</li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9">\n         <a href="#Regional_impacts">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Regional impacts\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10">\n           <a href="#Australia_and_the_Southern_Pacific">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Australia and the Southern Pacific\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11">\n           <a href="#Africa">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Africa\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12">\n           <a href="#Asia">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Asia\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a href="#Europe">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Europe\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14">\n           <a href="#North_America">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.5\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             North America\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15">\n           <a href="#South_America">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.6\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             South America\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16">\n         <a href="#Effects_on_humanity">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Effects on humanity\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17">\n           <a href="#Economic_effect">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Economic effect\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18">\n           <a href="#Health_and_social_effects">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Health and social effects\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20">\n         <a href="#Further_reading">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Further reading\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Concept">\n        Concept\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Concept">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Originally the term\n       <i>\n        El Ni\xc3\xb1o\n       </i>\n       applied to an annual weak warm ocean current that ran southwards along the coast of\n       <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">\n        Peru\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">\n        Ecuador\n       </a>\n       at about Christmas time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Definition_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Definition-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, over time the term has evolved and now refers to the warm and negative phase of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o_Southern_Oscillation" title="El Ni\xc3\xb1o Southern Oscillation">\n        El Ni\xc3\xb1o Southern Oscillation\n       </a>\n       and is the warming of the ocean surface or above-average sea surface temperatures in either the central and eastern tropical Pacific Ocean.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO:Nutshell_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO:Nutshell-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This warming causes a shift in the atmospheric circulation with rainfall becoming reduced over Indonesia and Australia, while rainfall and tropical cyclone formation increases over the tropical Pacific Ocean.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-What_is_an_El_Ni.C3.B1o.3F_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-What_is_an_El_Ni.C3.B1o.3F-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The low-level surface trade winds, which normally blow from east to west along the equator, either weaken or start blowing from the other direction.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO:Nutshell_9-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO:Nutshell-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Enso-index-map.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="305" data-file-width="918" height="66" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Enso-index-map.png/200px-Enso-index-map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Enso-index-map.png/300px-Enso-index-map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Enso-index-map.png/400px-Enso-index-map.png 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Enso-index-map.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Map showing Ni\xc3\xb1o3.4 and other index regions\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Historically, El Ni\xc3\xb1o events are thought to have been occurring for thousands of years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-El_Nino_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-El_Nino-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For example, it is thought that El Ni\xc3\xb1o affected the\n       <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">\n        Inca Empire\n       </a>\n       in modern-day\n       <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">\n        Peru\n       </a>\n       , who sacrificed humans in order to try to prevent the rains.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-El_Nino_11-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-El_Nino-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Scientists have also found the chemical signatures of warmer sea surface temperatures and increased rainfall caused by El Ni\xc3\xb1o in coral specimens that are around 13,000\xc2\xa0years old.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weather_Underground_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Weather_Underground-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In around 1525 when\n       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Pizarro" title="Francisco Pizarro">\n        Francisco Pizarro\n       </a>\n       made landfall on Peru, he noted rainfall occurring in the deserts which subsequently became the first written record of the impacts of El Ni\xc3\xb1o.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weather_Underground_12-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Weather_Underground-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Modern day research and reanalysis techniques have managed to find at least 26 El Ni\xc3\xb1o events since 1900, with the\n       <a href="/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_El_Ni%C3%B1o_event" title="1982\xe2\x80\x9383 El Ni\xc3\xb1o event">\n        1982-83\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_El_Ni%C3%B1o_event" title="1997\xe2\x80\x9398 El Ni\xc3\xb1o event">\n        1997\xe2\x80\x9398\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9316_El_Ni%C3%B1o_event" title="2014\xe2\x80\x9316 El Ni\xc3\xb1o event">\n        2014\xe2\x80\x9316\n       </a>\n       events among the strongest on record.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO_ONIs_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO_ONIs-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BoM_El_Nino_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BoM_El_Nino-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Currently, each country has a different threshold for what constitutes an El Ni\xc3\xb1o event, which is tailored to their specific interests.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-December_2014_EU_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-December_2014_EU-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For example, the Australian\n       <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Meteorology" title="Bureau of Meteorology">\n        Bureau of Meteorology\n       </a>\n       looks at the trade winds, SOI, weather models and sea surface temperatures in the Nino 3 and 3.4 regions, before declaring an El Ni\xc3\xb1o.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The United States Climate Prediction Center (CPC) and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Research_Institute_for_Climate_and_Society" title="International Research Institute for Climate and Society">\n        International Research Institute for Climate and Society\n       </a>\n       (IRI) looks at the sea surface temperatures in the Nino 3.4 region, the tropical Pacific atmosphere and forecasts that NOAA\'s Oceanic Ni\xc3\xb1o Index will equal or exceed +0.5\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C for several seasons in a row.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-How.3F_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-How.3F-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">\n        Japan Meteorological Agency\n       </a>\n       declares that an El Ni\xc3\xb1o event has started when the average 5 month sea surface temperature deviation for the NINO.3 region, is over 0.5\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (0.90\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) warmer for 6 consecutive months or longer.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Peruvian government declares that a coastal El Nino is under way, if the sea surface temperatures in the Nino 1 and 2 regions, equal or exceed +0.4\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C for at least 3 months.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There is no consensus on if climate change will have any influence on the occurrence, strength or duration of El Ni\xc3\xb1o events, as research supports El Ni\xc3\xb1o events becoming stronger, longer, shorter and weaker.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO_.2B_Climate_Change_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO_.2B_Climate_Change-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Collins10_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Collins10-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Occurrences">\n        Occurrences\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Occurrences">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <center>\n       <div class="timeline-wrapper">\n        <map id="timeline_748ba296fd5d729db6cb331b9609ad67" name="timeline_748ba296fd5d729db6cb331b9609ad67">\n        </map>\n        <img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/748ba296fd5d729db6cb331b9609ad67.png" usemap="#timeline_748ba296fd5d729db6cb331b9609ad67"/>\n       </div>\n       <p>\n        A timeline of all the El Ni\xc3\xb1o episodes between 1900 and 2016.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO_ONIs_13-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ENSO_ONIs-13">\n          [13]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BoM_El_Nino_14-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-BoM_El_Nino-14">\n          [14]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </p>\n      </center>\n      <p>\n       El Ni\xc3\xb1o events are thought to have been occurring for thousands of years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-El_Nino_11-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-El_Nino-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For example, it is thought that El Ni\xc3\xb1o affected the Inca Empire in modern-day Peru, who sacrificed humans in order to try and prevent the rains.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-El_Nino_11-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-El_Nino-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It is thought that there have been at least 30 El Ni\xc3\xb1o events since 1900, with the\n       <a href="/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_El_Ni%C3%B1o_event" title="1982\xe2\x80\x9383 El Ni\xc3\xb1o event">\n        1982-83\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_El_Ni%C3%B1o_event" title="1997\xe2\x80\x9398 El Ni\xc3\xb1o event">\n        1997\xe2\x80\x9398\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9316_El_Ni%C3%B1o_event" title="2014\xe2\x80\x9316 El Ni\xc3\xb1o event">\n        2014\xe2\x80\x9316\n       </a>\n       events among the strongest on record.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO_ONIs_13-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO_ONIs-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BoM_El_Nino_14-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BoM_El_Nino-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since 2000, El Ni\xc3\xb1o events have been observed in 2002\xe2\x80\x9303, 2004\xe2\x80\x9305, 2006\xe2\x80\x9307, 2009\xe2\x80\x9310 and\n       <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9316_El_Ni%C3%B1o_event" title="2014\xe2\x80\x9316 El Ni\xc3\xb1o event">\n        2014\xe2\x80\x9316\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO_ONIs_13-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO_ONIs-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Major ENSO events were recorded in the years 1790\xe2\x80\x9393, 1828, 1876\xe2\x80\x9378, 1891, 1925\xe2\x80\x9326, 1972\xe2\x80\x9373, 1982\xe2\x80\x9383, 1997\xe2\x80\x9398, and 2014\xe2\x80\x9316.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis2001_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Davis2001-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">\n          <span title="The material near this tag needs to be fact-checked with the cited source(s). (July 2015)">\n           verification needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">\n          <span title="sources are through 2001 (July 2015)">\n           needs update\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Typically, this anomaly happens at irregular intervals of two to seven years, and lasts nine months to two years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2005_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2005-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The average period length is five years. When this warming occurs for seven to nine months, it is classified as El Ni\xc3\xb1o "conditions"; when its duration is longer, it is classified as an El Ni\xc3\xb1o "episode".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-administration1_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-administration1-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There is no consensus on whether climate change will have any influence on the occurrence, strength or duration of El Ni\xc3\xb1o events, as research supports El Ni\xc3\xb1o events becoming stronger, longer, shorter and weaker.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO_.2B_Climate_Change_20-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO_.2B_Climate_Change-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Collins10_21-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Collins10-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During strong El Ni\xc3\xb1o episodes, a secondary peak in sea surface temperature across the far eastern equatorial Pacific Ocean sometimes follows the initial peak.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_history_and_prehistoric_information">\n        Cultural history and prehistoric information\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Cultural history and prehistoric information">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mean_sst_equatorial_pacific.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="645" data-file-width="432" height="299" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Mean_sst_equatorial_pacific.gif/200px-Mean_sst_equatorial_pacific.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Mean_sst_equatorial_pacific.gif/300px-Mean_sst_equatorial_pacific.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Mean_sst_equatorial_pacific.gif/400px-Mean_sst_equatorial_pacific.gif 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mean_sst_equatorial_pacific.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Average equatorial Pacific temperatures\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       ENSO conditions have occurred at two- to seven-year intervals for at least the past 300 years, but most of them have been weak. Evidence is also strong for El Ni\xc3\xb1o events during the early\n       <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">\n        Holocene\n       </a>\n       epoch 10,000 years ago.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       El Ni\xc3\xb1o may have led to the demise of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moche_(culture)" title="Moche (culture)">\n        Moche\n       </a>\n       and other pre-Columbian\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cultural_periods_of_Peru" title="Cultural periods of Peru">\n        Peruvian cultures\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A recent study suggests a strong El-Ni\xc3\xb1o effect between 1789 and 1793 caused poor crop yields in Europe, which in turn helped touch off the\n       <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">\n        French Revolution\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grove1998_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Grove1998-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The extreme weather produced by El Ni\xc3\xb1o in 1876\xe2\x80\x9377 gave rise to the most deadly\n       <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">\n        famines\n       </a>\n       of the 19th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Chinese_Famine_of_1876%E2%80%931879" title="Northern Chinese Famine of 1876\xe2\x80\x931879">\n        1876 famine\n       </a>\n       alone in northern China killed up to 13 million people.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       An early recorded mention of the term "El Ni\xc3\xb1o" to refer to climate occurred in 1892, when\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camilo_Carrillo_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="es:Camilo Carrillo Mart\xc3\xadnez">\n        Captain Camilo Carrillo\n       </a>\n       told the geographical society congress in\n       <a href="/wiki/Lima" title="Lima">\n        Lima\n       </a>\n       that Peruvian sailors named the warm north-flowing current "El Ni\xc3\xb1o" because it was most noticeable around Christmas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The phenomenon had long been of interest because of its effects on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Guano" title="Guano">\n        guano\n       </a>\n       industry and other enterprises that depend on biological productivity of the sea.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_Todd_(astronomer)" title="Charles Todd (astronomer)">\n        Charles Todd\n       </a>\n       , in 1888, suggested droughts in India and Australia tended to occur at the same time;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Norman_Lockyer" title="Norman Lockyer">\n        Norman Lockyer\n       </a>\n       noted the same in 1904.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An El Ni\xc3\xb1o connection with flooding was reported in 1894 by\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=V%C3%ADctor_Eguiguren_Escudero&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="V\xc3\xadctor Eguiguren Escudero (page does not exist)">\n        V\xc3\xadctor Eguiguren\n       </a>\n       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">\n        (\n        <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/V%C3%ADctor_Eguiguren_Escudero" title="es:V\xc3\xadctor Eguiguren Escudero">\n         es\n        </a>\n        )\n       </span>\n       (1852\xe2\x80\x931919) and in 1895 by Federico Alfonso Pezet (1859\xe2\x80\x931929).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1924,\n       <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Walker" title="Gilbert Walker">\n        Gilbert Walker\n       </a>\n       (for whom the\n       <a href="/wiki/Walker_circulation" title="Walker circulation">\n        Walker circulation\n       </a>\n       is named) coined the term "Southern Oscillation".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       He and others (including Norwegian-American meteorologist\n       <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Bjerknes" title="Jacob Bjerknes">\n        Jacob Bjerknes\n       </a>\n       ) are generally credited with identifying the El Ni\xc3\xb1o effect.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The major 1982\xe2\x80\x9383 El Ni\xc3\xb1o led to an upsurge of interest from the scientific community. The period 1991\xe2\x80\x931995 was unusual in that El Ni\xc3\xb1os have rarely occurred in such rapid succession.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trenberth1996_40-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Trenberth1996-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An especially intense El Ni\xc3\xb1o event in 1998 caused an estimated 16% of the world\'s reef systems to die. The event temporarily warmed air temperature by 1.5\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C, compared to the usual increase of 0.25\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C associated with El Ni\xc3\xb1o events.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trenberth_41-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Trenberth-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since then, mass\n       <a href="/wiki/Coral_bleaching" title="Coral bleaching">\n        coral bleaching\n       </a>\n       has become common worldwide, with all regions having suffered "severe bleaching".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall2006_42-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Marshall2006-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Diversity">\n        Diversity\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Diversity">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Enso-index-map.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="305" data-file-width="918" height="66" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Enso-index-map.png/200px-Enso-index-map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Enso-index-map.png/300px-Enso-index-map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Enso-index-map.png/400px-Enso-index-map.png 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Enso-index-map.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Map showing Ni\xc3\xb1o3.4 and other index regions\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       It is thought that there are several different types of El Ni\xc3\xb1o events, with the canonical eastern Pacific and the Modoki central Pacific types being the two that receive the most attention.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO_Flavors_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO_Flavors-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO:Flavor_45-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO:Flavor-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These different types of El Ni\xc3\xb1o events are classified by where the tropical Pacific sea surface temperature (SST) anomalies are the largest.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO:Flavor_45-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO:Flavor-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For example, the strongest sea surface temperature anomalies associated with the canonical eastern Pacific event are located off the coast of South America.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO:Flavor_45-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO:Flavor-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The strongest anomalies associated with the Modoki central Pacific event are located near the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Dateline" title="International Dateline">\n        International Dateline\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO:Flavor_45-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO:Flavor-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, during the duration of a single event, the area with the greatest sea surface temperature anomalies can change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO:Flavor_45-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO:Flavor-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The traditional Ni\xc3\xb1o, also called Eastern Pacific (EP) El Ni\xc3\xb1o,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yu2009_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Yu2009-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       involves temperature anomalies in the Eastern Pacific. However, in the last two decades, nontraditional El Ni\xc3\xb1os were observed, in which the usual place of the temperature anomaly (Ni\xc3\xb1o 1 and 2) is not affected, but an anomaly arises in the central Pacific (Ni\xc3\xb1o 3.4).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Larkin2007_47-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Larkin2007-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The phenomenon is called Central Pacific (CP) El Ni\xc3\xb1o,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yu2009_46-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Yu2009-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       "dateline" El Ni\xc3\xb1o (because the anomaly arises near the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_dateline" title="International dateline">\n        dateline\n       </a>\n       ), or El Ni\xc3\xb1o "Modoki" (Modoki is\n       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">\n        Japanese\n       </a>\n       for "similar, but different").\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The effects of the CP El Ni\xc3\xb1o are different from those of the traditional EP El Ni\xc3\xb1o\xe2\x80\x94e.g., the recently discovered El Ni\xc3\xb1o leads to more hurricanes more frequently making landfall in the Atlantic.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kim2009_52-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kim2009-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There is also a scientific debate on the very existence of this "new" ENSO. Indeed, a number of studies dispute the reality of this statistical distinction or its increasing occurrence, or both, either arguing the reliable record is too short to detect such a distinction,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       finding no distinction or trend using other statistical approaches,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       or that other types should be distinguished, such as standard and extreme ENSO.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The first recorded El Ni\xc3\xb1o that originated in the central Pacific and moved toward the east was in 1986.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Recent Central Pacific El Ni\xc3\xb1os happened in 1986\xe2\x80\x9387, 1991\xe2\x80\x9392, 1994\xe2\x80\x9395, 2002\xe2\x80\x9303, 2004\xe2\x80\x9305 and 2009\xe2\x80\x9310.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Furthermore, there were "Modoki" events in 1957\xe2\x80\x9359,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       1963\xe2\x80\x9364, 1965\xe2\x80\x9366, 1968\xe2\x80\x9370, 1977\xe2\x80\x9378 and 1979\xe2\x80\x9380.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_the_global_climate">\n        Effects on the global climate\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Effects on the global climate">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       El Nino affects the global climate and disrupts normal weather patterns, which as a result can lead to intense storms in some places and droughts in others.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIWA_El_Ni.C3.B1o.2FLa_Ni.C3.B1a_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIWA_El_Ni.C3.B1o.2FLa_Ni.C3.B1a-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_cyclones">\n        Tropical cyclones\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tropical cyclones">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Most tropical cyclones form on the side of the subtropical ridge closer to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">\n        equator\n       </a>\n       , then move poleward past the ridge axis before recurving into the main belt of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Westerlies" title="Westerlies">\n        Westerlies\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Areas west of\n       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">\n        Japan\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">\n        Korea\n       </a>\n       tend to experience much fewer September\xe2\x80\x93November tropical cyclone impacts during El Ni\xc3\xb1o and neutral years. During El Ni\xc3\xb1o years, the break in the subtropical ridge tends to lie near\n       <a href="/wiki/130th_meridian_east" title="130th meridian east">\n        130\xc2\xb0E\n       </a>\n       , which would favor the Japanese archipelago.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-China_70-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-China-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Within the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_basins#Atlantic_Ocean" title="Tropical cyclone basins">\n        Atlantic Ocean\n       </a>\n       vertical wind shear is increased, which inhibits tropical cyclone genesis and intensification, by causing the westerly winds in the atmosphere to be stronger.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TC_FAQ_G2_71-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TC_FAQ_G2-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The atmosphere over the Atlantic Ocean can also be drier and more stable during El Ni\xc3\xb1o events, which can also inhibit tropical cyclone genesis and intensification.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TC_FAQ_G2_71-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TC_FAQ_G2-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Within the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_basins#Eastern_Pacific" title="Tropical cyclone basins">\n        Eastern Pacific basin\n       </a>\n       : El Ni\xc3\xb1o events contribute to decreased easterly vertical wind shear and favours above-normal hurricane activity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_Background_72-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EPAC_Background-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, the impacts of the ENSO state in this region can vary and are strongly influenced by background climate patterns.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_Background_72-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EPAC_Background-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_basins#Western_Pacific" title="Tropical cyclone basins">\n        Western Pacific basin\n       </a>\n       experiences a change in the location of where tropical cyclones form during El Ni\xc3\xb1o events, without a major change in how many develop each year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TC_FAQ_G2_71-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TC_FAQ_G2-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">\n        As a result of this change Micronesia is more likely to be affected by several tropical cyclones, while China has a decreased risk of being affected by several tropical cyclones.\n       </span>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       A change in the location of where tropical cyclones form also occurs within the Southern Pacific Ocean between 135\xc2\xb0E and 120\xc2\xb0W, with tropical cyclones more likely to occur within the Southern Pacific basin than the Australian region.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-What_is_an_El_Ni.C3.B1o.3F_10-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-What_is_an_El_Ni.C3.B1o.3F-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TC_FAQ_G2_71-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TC_FAQ_G2-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As a result of this change tropical cyclones are 50% less likely to make landfall on Queensland, while the risk of a tropical cyclone is elevated for island nations like\n       <a href="/wiki/Niue" title="Niue">\n        Niue\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">\n        French Polynesia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tonga" title="Tonga">\n        Tonga\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">\n        Tuvalu\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">\n        Cook Islands\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-What_is_an_El_Ni.C3.B1o.3F_10-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-What_is_an_El_Ni.C3.B1o.3F-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIWA_73-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIWA-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Remote_influence_on_tropical_Atlantic_Ocean">\n        Remote influence on tropical Atlantic Ocean\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Remote influence on tropical Atlantic Ocean">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       A study of climate records has shown that El Ni\xc3\xb1o events in the equatorial Pacific are generally associated with a warm tropical North Atlantic in the following spring and summer.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       About half of El Ni\xc3\xb1o events persist sufficiently into the spring months for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere_Warm_Pool" title="Western Hemisphere Warm Pool">\n        Western Hemisphere Warm Pool\n       </a>\n       to become unusually large in summer.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Occasionally, El Ni\xc3\xb1o\'s effect on the Atlantic Walker circulation over South America strengthens the easterly trade winds in the western equatorial Atlantic region. As a result, an unusual cooling may occur in the eastern equatorial Atlantic in spring and summer following El Ni\xc3\xb1o peaks in winter.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Cases of El Ni\xc3\xb1o-type events in both oceans simultaneously have been linked to severe\n       <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">\n        famines\n       </a>\n       related to the extended failure of\n       <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">\n        monsoon\n       </a>\n       rains.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis2001_22-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Davis2001-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Antarctica">\n        Antarctica\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Antarctica">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Many ENSO linkages exist in the high southern latitudes around\n       <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">\n        Antarctica\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Turner2004_78-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Turner2004-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Specifically, El Ni\xc3\xb1o conditions result in\n       <a href="/wiki/High-pressure_area" title="High-pressure area">\n        high-pressure\n       </a>\n       anomalies over the\n       <a href="/wiki/Amundsen_Sea" title="Amundsen Sea">\n        Amundsen\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Bellingshausen_Sea" title="Bellingshausen Sea">\n        Bellingshausen\n       </a>\n       Seas, causing reduced\n       <a href="/wiki/Sea_ice" title="Sea ice">\n        sea ice\n       </a>\n       and increased poleward heat fluxes in these sectors, as well as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ross_Sea" title="Ross Sea">\n        Ross Sea\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Weddell_Sea" title="Weddell Sea">\n        Weddell Sea\n       </a>\n       , conversely, tends to become colder with more sea ice during El Ni\xc3\xb1o. The exact opposite heating and atmospheric pressure anomalies occur during La Ni\xc3\xb1a.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yuan2004_79-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Yuan2004-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This pattern of variability is known as the Antarctic dipole mode, although the Antarctic response to ENSO forcing is not ubiquitous.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yuan2004_79-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Yuan2004-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_impacts">\n        Regional impacts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Regional impacts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Observations of El Ni\xc3\xb1o events since 1950, show that impacts associated with El Ni\xc3\xb1o events depend on what season it is.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cascade_80-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cascade-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, while certain events and impacts are expected to occur during events, it is not certain or guaranteed that they will occur.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cascade_80-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cascade-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The impacts that generally do occur during most El Ni\xc3\xb1o events include below-average rainfall over Indonesia and northern South America, while above average rainfall occurs in southeastern South America, eastern equatorial Africa, and the southern United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cascade_80-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cascade-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Australia_and_the_Southern_Pacific">\n        Australia and the Southern Pacific\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Australia and the Southern Pacific">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       During El Ni\xc3\xb1o events, the shift in rainfall away from the Western Pacific may mean that rainfall across Australia is reduced.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-What_is_an_El_Ni.C3.B1o.3F_10-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-What_is_an_El_Ni.C3.B1o.3F-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Over the southern part of the continent, warmer than average temperatures can be recorded as weather systems are more mobile and fewer blocking areas of high pressure occur.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-What_is_an_El_Ni.C3.B1o.3F_10-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-What_is_an_El_Ni.C3.B1o.3F-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The onset of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Monsoon#Australia" title="Monsoon">\n        Indo-Australian Monsoon\n       </a>\n       in tropical Australia is delayed by two to six weeks, which as a consequence means that rainfall is reduced over the northern tropics.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-What_is_an_El_Ni.C3.B1o.3F_10-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-What_is_an_El_Ni.C3.B1o.3F-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The risk of a significant bushfire season in south-eastern Australia is higher following an El Ni\xc3\xb1o event, especially when it is combined with a positive\n       <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_Dipole" title="Indian Ocean Dipole">\n        Indian Ocean Dipole\n       </a>\n       event.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-What_is_an_El_Ni.C3.B1o.3F_10-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-What_is_an_El_Ni.C3.B1o.3F-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During an El Ni\xc3\xb1o event, New Zealand tends to experience stronger or more frequent westerly winds during their summer, which leads to an elevated risk of drier than normal conditions along the east coast.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Zealand_El_Ni.C3.B1o.27s_impacts_81-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-New_Zealand_El_Ni.C3.B1o.27s_impacts-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There is more rain than usual though on New Zealand\'s West Coast, because of the barrier effect of the North Island mountain ranges and the Southern Alps.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Zealand_El_Ni.C3.B1o.27s_impacts_81-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-New_Zealand_El_Ni.C3.B1o.27s_impacts-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Fiji generally experiences drier than normal conditions during an El Ni\xc3\xb1o, which can lead to drought becoming established over the Islands.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fiji_ENSO_Update_82-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Fiji_ENSO_Update-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, the main impacts on the island nation is felt about a year after the event becomes established.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fiji_ENSO_Update_82-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Fiji_ENSO_Update-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Within the Samoan Islands, below average rainfall and higher than normal temperatures are recorded during El Ni\xc3\xb1o events, which can lead to droughts and forest fires on the islands.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clim_Jan_2016_83-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Clim_Jan_2016-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Other impacts include a decrease in the sea level, possibility of coral bleaching in the marine environment and an increased risk of a tropical cyclone affecting Samoa.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clim_Jan_2016_83-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Clim_Jan_2016-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">\n        Africa\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Africa">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In Africa,\n       <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">\n        East Africa\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94 including\n       <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">\n        Kenya\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">\n        Tanzania\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/White_Nile" title="White Nile">\n        White Nile\n       </a>\n       basin\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 experiences, in the long rains from March to May, wetter-than-normal conditions. Conditions are also drier than normal from December to February in south-central Africa, mainly in\n       <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">\n        Zambia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">\n        Zimbabwe\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">\n        Mozambique\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">\n        Botswana\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">\n        Asia\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Asia">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       As warm water spreads from the west Pacific and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">\n        Indian Ocean\n       </a>\n       to the east Pacific, it takes the rain with it, causing extensive drought in the western Pacific and rainfall in the normally dry eastern Pacific. Singapore experienced the driest February in 2014 since records began in 1869, with only 6.3\xc2\xa0mm of rain falling in the month and temperatures hitting as high as 35\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C on 26 February. The years 1968 and 2005 had the next driest Februaries, when 8.4\xc2\xa0mm of rain fell.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">\n        Europe\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Europe">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       El Ni\xc3\xb1o\'s effects on\n       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">\n        Europe\n       </a>\n       are controversial, complex and difficult to analyse, as it is one of several factors that influence the weather over the continent and other factors can overwhelm the signal.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n        <a href="#cite_note-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">\n        North America\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: North America">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:258px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:El_Nino_regional_impacts.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="539" data-file-width="486" height="284" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/El_Nino_regional_impacts.png/256px-El_Nino_regional_impacts.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/El_Nino_regional_impacts.png/384px-El_Nino_regional_impacts.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b7/El_Nino_regional_impacts.png 2x" width="256"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:El_Nino_regional_impacts.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Regional impacts of warm ENSO episodes (El Ni\xc3\xb1o)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_the_El_Ni%C3%B1o%E2%80%93Southern_Oscillation_in_the_United_States" title="Effects of the El Ni\xc3\xb1o\xe2\x80\x93Southern Oscillation in the United States">\n        Effects of the El Ni\xc3\xb1o\xe2\x80\x93Southern Oscillation in the United States\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Over North America, the main temperature and precipitation impacts of El Ni\xc3\xb1o, generally occur in the six months between October and March.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO:Impacts_87-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO:Impacts-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climate_impacts_88-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-climate_impacts-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In particular the majority of Canada generally has a milder than normal winters and cold fronts springs, with the exception of eastern Canada where no significant impacts occur.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Within the United States, the impacts generally observed during the six-month period include; wetter-than-average conditions along the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast" title="Gulf Coast">\n        Gulf Coast\n       </a>\n       between\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">\n        Texas\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">\n        Florida\n       </a>\n       , while drier conditions are observed in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">\n        Hawaii\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ohio_Valley" title="Ohio Valley">\n        Ohio Valley\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">\n        Pacific Northwest\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">\n        Rocky Mountains\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO:Impacts_87-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO:Impacts-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Over California and the South-Western United States, there is a weak relationship between El Nino and above-average precipitation, as it strongly depends on the strength of the El Ni\xc3\xb1o event amongst other factors.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENSO:Impacts_87-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ENSO:Impacts-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Synoptic_scale_meteorology" title="Synoptic scale meteorology">\n        synoptic\n       </a>\n       condition for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tehuantepecer" title="Tehuantepecer">\n        Tehuantepecer\n       </a>\n       is associated with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-pressure_system" title="High-pressure system">\n        high-pressure system\n       </a>\n       forming in\n       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_de_Oaxaca" title="Sierra Madre de Oaxaca">\n        Sierra Madre\n       </a>\n       of Mexico in the wake of an advancing cold front, which causes winds to accelerate through the\n       <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Tehuantepec" title="Isthmus of Tehuantepec">\n        Isthmus of Tehuantepec\n       </a>\n       . Tehuantepecers primarily occur during the cold season months for the region in the wake of cold fronts, between October and February, with a summer maximum in July caused by the westward extension of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Azores_High" title="Azores High">\n        Azores High\n       </a>\n       . Wind magnitude is greater during El Ni\xc3\xb1o years than during\n       <a href="/wiki/La_Ni%C3%B1a" title="La Ni\xc3\xb1a">\n        La Ni\xc3\xb1a\n       </a>\n       years, due to the more frequent cold frontal incursions during El Ni\xc3\xb1o winters.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n        <a href="#cite_note-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Its effects can last from a few hours to six days.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWL1971_91-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MWL1971-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="South_America">\n        South America\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: South America">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Because El Ni\xc3\xb1o\'s warm pool feeds thunderstorms above, it creates increased rainfall across the east-central and eastern Pacific Ocean, including several portions of the South American west coast. The effects of El Ni\xc3\xb1o in South America are direct and stronger than in North America. An El Ni\xc3\xb1o is associated with warm and very wet weather months in April\xe2\x80\x93October along the coasts of northern\n       <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">\n        Peru\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">\n        Ecuador\n       </a>\n       , causing major flooding whenever the event is strong or extreme.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The effects during the months of February, March, and April may become critical. Along the west coast of\n       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">\n        South America\n       </a>\n       , El Ni\xc3\xb1o reduces the upwelling of cold, nutrient-rich water that sustains large\n       <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">\n        fish\n       </a>\n       populations, which in turn sustain abundant sea birds, whose droppings support the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">\n        fertilizer\n       </a>\n       industry. The reduction in upwelling leads to\n       <a href="/wiki/Fish_kill" title="Fish kill">\n        fish kills\n       </a>\n       off the shore of Peru.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deadfish_93-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-deadfish-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The local fishing industry along the affected coastline can suffer during long-lasting El Ni\xc3\xb1o events. The world\'s largest fishery collapsed due to overfishing during the 1972 El Ni\xc3\xb1o\n       <a href="/wiki/Peruvian_anchoveta" title="Peruvian anchoveta">\n        Peruvian anchoveta\n       </a>\n       reduction. During the 1982\xe2\x80\x9383 event,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mackerel" title="Mackerel">\n        jack mackerel\n       </a>\n       and anchoveta populations were reduced,\n       <a href="/wiki/Scallop" title="Scallop">\n        scallops\n       </a>\n       increased in warmer water, but\n       <a href="/wiki/Hake" title="Hake">\n        hake\n       </a>\n       followed cooler water down the continental slope, while\n       <a href="/wiki/Shrimp" title="Shrimp">\n        shrimp\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sardines" title="Sardines">\n        sardines\n       </a>\n       moved southward, so some catches decreased while others increased.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pearcy1987_94-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Pearcy1987-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Mackerel" title="Mackerel">\n        Horse mackerel\n       </a>\n       have increased in the region during warm events. Shifting locations and types of fish due to changing conditions provide challenges for fishing industries. Peruvian\n       <a href="/wiki/Sardine" title="Sardine">\n        sardines\n       </a>\n       have moved during El Ni\xc3\xb1o events to\n       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">\n        Chilean\n       </a>\n       areas. Other conditions provide further complications, such as the government of Chile in 1991 creating restrictions on the fishing areas for self-employed fishermen and industrial fleets.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The ENSO variability may contribute to the great success of small, fast-growing species along the Peruvian coast, as periods of low population removes predators in the area. Similar effects benefit\n       <a href="/wiki/Bird_migration" title="Bird migration">\n        migratory\n       </a>\n       birds that travel each spring from predator-rich tropical areas to distant winter-stressed nesting areas.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Southern\n       <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">\n        Brazil\n       </a>\n       and northern\n       <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">\n        Argentina\n       </a>\n       also experience wetter than normal conditions, but mainly during the spring and early summer. Central Chile receives a mild winter with large rainfall, and the Peruvian-Bolivian\n       <a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">\n        Altiplano\n       </a>\n       is sometimes exposed to unusual winter snowfall events. Drier and hotter weather occurs in parts of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">\n        Amazon River\n       </a>\n       Basin,\n       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">\n        Colombia\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">\n        Central America\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_humanity">\n        Effects on humanity\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Effects on humanity">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_effect">\n        Economic effect\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economic effect">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ElNinoBloom_1998JanJul.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="720" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/ElNinoBloom_1998JanJul.gif/220px-ElNinoBloom_1998JanJul.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/ElNinoBloom_1998JanJul.gif/330px-ElNinoBloom_1998JanJul.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/ElNinoBloom_1998JanJul.gif/440px-ElNinoBloom_1998JanJul.gif 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ElNinoBloom_1998JanJul.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         El Ni\xc3\xb1o has the most direct impacts on life in the equatorial Pacific, its effects propagate north and south along the coast of the Americas, affecting marine life all around the Pacific. Changes in chlorophyll-a concentrations are visible in this animation, which compares\n         <a href="/wiki/Phytoplankton" title="Phytoplankton">\n          phytoplankton\n         </a>\n         in January and July 1998. Since then, scientists have improved both the collection and presentation of\n         <a href="/wiki/Chlorophyll" title="Chlorophyll">\n          chlorophyll\n         </a>\n         data.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       When El Ni\xc3\xb1o conditions last for many months, extensive ocean warming and the reduction in easterly trade winds limits upwelling of cold nutrient-rich deep water, and its economic effect on local fishing for an international market can be serious.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deadfish_93-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-deadfish-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       More generally, El Ni\xc3\xb1o can affect commodity prices and the macroeconomy of different countries. It can constrain the supply of rain-driven agricultural commodities; reduce agricultural output, construction, and services activities; create food-price and generalised inflation; and may trigger social unrest in commodity-dependent poor countries that primarily rely on imported food.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-University_of_Cambridge_95-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-University_of_Cambridge-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A University of Cambridge Working Paper shows that while Australia, Chile, Indonesia, India, Japan, New Zealand and South Africa face a short-lived fall in economic activity in response to an El Ni\xc3\xb1o shock, other countries may actually benefit from an El Ni\xc3\xb1o weather shock (either directly or indirectly through positive spillovers from major trading partners), for instance, Argentina, Canada, Mexico and the United States. Furthermore, most countries experience short-run inflationary pressures following an El Ni\xc3\xb1o shock, while global energy and non-fuel commodity prices increase.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The IMF estimates a significant El Ni\xc3\xb1o can boost the GDP of the United States by about 0.5% (due largely to lower heating bills) and reduce the GDP of Indonesia by about 1.0%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health_and_social_effects">\n        Health and social effects\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ni%C3%B1o&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Health and social effects">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Extreme weather conditions related to the El Ni\xc3\xb1o cycle correlate with changes in the incidence of\n       <a href="/wiki/Epidemic" title="Epidemic">\n        epidemic\n       </a>\n       diseases. For example, the El Ni\xc3\xb1o cycle is associated with increased risks of some of the diseases transmitted by\n       <a href="/wiki/Mosquito" title="Mosquito">\n        mosquitoes\n       </a>\n       , such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">\n        malaria\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dengue" title="Dengue">\n        dengue\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Rift_Valley_fever" title="Rift Valley fever">\n        Rift Valley fever\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">\n        <a href="#cite_note-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       . Cycles of malaria in\n       <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">\n        India\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">\n        Venezuela\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">\n        Brazil\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">\n        Colombia\n       </a>\n       have now been linked to El Ni\xc3\xb1o. Outbreaks of another mosquito-transmitted disease, Australian encephalitis (\n       <a href="/wiki/Murray_Valley_encephalitis_virus" title="Murray Valley encephalitis virus">\n        Murray Valley encephalitis\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94MVE), occur in temperate south-east Australia after heavy rainfall and flooding, which are associated with La Ni\xc3\xb1a events. A severe outbreak of Rift Valley fever occurred after extreme rainfall in north-eastern Kenya and southern Somalia during the 1997\xe2\x80\x9398 El Ni\xc3\xb1o.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">\n        <a href="#cite_note-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       ENSO conditions have also been related to\n       <a href="/wiki/Kawasaki_disease" title="Kawasaki disease">\n        Kawasaki disease\n       </a>\n       incidence in Japan and the west coast of the United States,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ballester_100-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ballester-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       via the linkage to tropospheric winds across the north Pacific Ocean.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rod_101-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rod-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       ENSO may be linked to civil conflicts. Scientists at\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Earth_Institute" title="The Earth Institute">\n        The Earth Institute\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">\n        Columbia University\n       </a>\n       , having analyzed data from 1950 to 2004, suggest ENSO may have had a role in 21% of all civil conflicts since 1950, with the risk of annual civil conflict doubling from 3% to 6% in countries affected by ENSO during El Ni\xc3\xb1o years relative to La Ni\xc3\xb1a years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">\n        <a href="#cite_note-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n        <a href="#cite_note-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="References">\n        References\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n       <div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns">\n        <ol class="references">\n         <li id="cite_note-1">\n          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n           <b>\n            <a href="#cite_ref-1">\n             ^\n            </a>\n           </b>\n          </span>\n          <span class="reference-text">\n           <cite class="citation web">\n            <a class="external text" href="http://www.jpl.nasa.gov/news/releases/97/elninoup.html" rel="nofollow">\n             "Independent NASA Satellite Measurements Confirm El Ni\xc3\xb1o is Back and Strong"\n            </a>\n     </a>\n            .\n           </cite>\n           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEl+Ni%C3%B1o&amp;rft.btitle=Independent+NASA+Satellite+Measurements+Confirm+El+Ni%C3%B1o+is+Back+and+Strong&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.pub=NASA%2FJPL&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.jpl.nasa.gov%2Fnews%2Freleases%2F97%2Felninoup.html&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">\n            <span style="display:none;">\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </li>\n         <li id="cite_note-CPC_ENSO-2">\n          <span
